<p>Paul is a proponent of <a href="/wiki/Austrian_School" title="Austrian School">Austrian School</a> economics; he has authored six books on the subject, and displays pictures of Austrian School economists <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray_Rothbard" title="Murray Rothbard">Murray Rothbard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_von_Mises" title="Ludwig von Mises">Ludwig von Mises</a> (as well as of President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-will_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-will-152">[152]</a></sup> on his office wall. He regularly votes against almost all proposals for new government spending, initiatives, or taxes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saynot_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-saynot-153">[153]</a></sup> he cast two thirds of all the lone negative votes in the House during a 1995–1997 period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drno_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-drno-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>He has pledged never to raise taxes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> and states he has never voted to approve a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a>. Paul believes that the country could abolish the individual income tax by scaling back federal spending to its fiscal year 2000 levels;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endirs_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-endirs-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> financing government operations would be primarily by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excise_taxes_(U.S.)" title="Excise taxes (U.S.)">excise taxes</a> and non-protectionist <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>. He endorses eliminating most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_agencies#Government_agencies_in_the_United_States" title="Government agencies">federal government agencies</a>, terming them unnecessary bureaucracies.</p>
<p>On April 15, 2011, Paul was one of four Republican members of Congress to vote against Rep. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ryan" title="Paul Ryan">Paul Ryan</a>'s budget proposal, known as "<a href="/wiki/The_Path_to_Prosperity" title="The Path to Prosperity">The Path to Prosperity</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul has consistently warned of <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflation</a> as far back as 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> While Paul believes the longterm decrease of the U.S. dollar's purchasing power by <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> is attributable to its lack of any commodity backing, he does not endorse a "return" to a <a href="/wiki/Gold_standard" title="Gold standard">gold standard</a> – as the U.S. government has established during the past – but instead prefers to eliminate <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> laws and to remove the sales tax on gold and silver, so that the market may freely decide what type of monetary standard(s) there shall be.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Since 1999, he has introduced bills into each Congress seeking to eliminate the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System" title="Federal Reserve System">Federal Reserve System</a> in a single year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>He endorses <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>, rejecting membership in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> as "managed trade".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">Environmental</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environmental">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free-market_environmentalist" title="Free-market environmentalist">free-market environmentalist</a>, he asserts <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a> rights in relation to environmental protection and pollution prevention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> He called <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> a hoax in a 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_Business" title="Fox Business">Fox Business</a> interview, saying, "You know, the greatest hoax I think that has been around in many, many years if not hundreds of years has been this hoax on the environment and global warming."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> He acknowledges there is clear evidence of rising temperatures in some parts of the globe, but says that temperatures are cooling in other parts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Paul has stated that "The government shouldn't be in the medical business." He pushes to eliminate federal involvement with and management of <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_the_United_States" title="Health care in the United States">health care</a>, which he argues would allow prices to decrease due to the fundamental dynamics of a free market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> He also opposes federal government influenza <a href="/wiki/Inoculation" title="Inoculation">inoculation</a> programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Paul endorses increased border security and opposes welfare for <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">illegal aliens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anchor_baby" title="Anchor baby">birthright citizenship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> he voted for the <a href="/wiki/Secure_Fence_Act_of_2006" title="Secure Fence Act of 2006">Secure Fence Act of 2006</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ballots_and_voting">Ballots and voting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Ballots and voting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He is an outspoken proponent of increased <a href="/wiki/Ballot_access" title="Ballot access">ballot access</a> for third-party candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> He has sought to repeal the <a href="/wiki/National_Voter_Registration_Act_of_1993" title="National Voter Registration Act of 1993">National Voter Registration Act of 1993</a>, also known as the Motor Voter law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secession">Secession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Secession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Paul has stated that <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> from the United States "is a deeply American principle" and that "If the possibility of secession is completely off the table there is nothing to stop the federal government from continuing to encroach on our liberties and no recourse for those who are sick and tired of it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Paul wrote the remarks in a post on his Congressional website in one of his final public statements as a member of Congress, noting that <a href="/wiki/2012_state_petitions_for_secession" title="2012 state petitions for secession">many petitions</a> had been submitted to the White House calling for secession in the wake of the November 2012 election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Social issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He terms himself "strongly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">pro-life</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> "an unshakable foe of abortion",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> and believes regulation or ban<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> on medical decisions about maternal or fetal health is "best handled at the state level".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanview_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-americanview-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> His abortion-related legislation, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sanctity_of_Life_Act" title="Sanctity of Life Act">Sanctity of Life Act</a>, is intended to negate <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i> and to get "the federal government completely out of the business of regulating state matters."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Paul says his years as an obstetrician led him to believe life begins at <a href="/wiki/Fertilisation" title="Fertilisation">conception</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul opposes the federal <a href="/wiki/War_on_Drugs" title="War on Drugs">War on Drugs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and believes the states should decide whether to regulate or deregulate drugs such as <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis_in_the_United_States" title="Medical cannabis in the United States">medical marijuana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Citing the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Ninth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Ninth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Tenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Tenth Amendments</a>, Paul advocates <a href="/wiki/States%27_rights" title="States' rights">states' rights</a> to decide how to regulate social matters not cited directly by the Constitution. He opposes federal regulation of the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_United_States" title="Capital punishment in the United States">death penalty</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanview_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-americanview-176">[176]</a></sup> (although he opposes capital punishment),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> of education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> and of marriage, and endorsed revising the military's "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don't ask, don't tell">don't ask, don't tell</a>" policy to concern mainly disruptive sexual behavior (whether heterosexual or homosexual).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul was critical of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>, arguing that it sanctioned federal interference in the labor market and did not improve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_relations" title="Race relations">race relations</a>. He once remarked: "The Civil Rights Act of 1964 not only violated the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a> and reduced individual liberty; it also failed to achieve its stated goals of promoting racial harmony and a color-blind society".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cr1964_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-cr1964-185">[185]</a></sup> Paul opposes <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action_in_the_United_States" title="Affirmative action in the United States">affirmative action</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Newsletters_controversy">Newsletters controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Newsletters controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul_newsletters" title="Ron Paul newsletters">Ron Paul newsletters</a></div>
<p>Beginning in 1978, for more than two decades Paul and his associates published a number of political and investment-oriented newsletters bearing his name (<i>Dr. Ron Paul's Freedom Report</i>, <i>The Ron Paul Survival Report</i>, the <i>Ron Paul Investment Letter</i>, and the <i>Ron Paul Political Report</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChickAWM_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChickAWM-187">[187]</a></sup> By 1993, a business through which Paul was publishing the newsletters was earning in excess of $900,000 per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChickAWM_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-ChickAWM-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of the newsletters, particularly in the period between 1988 and 1994 when Paul was no longer in Congress, contained material that later proved controversial. Topics included on conspiracy theories, anti-government militia movements, and race wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChickAWM_187-2"><a href="#cite_note-ChickAWM-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNR120117_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-TNR120117-188">[188]</a></sup> During Paul's 1996 congressional election campaign, and his 2008 and 2012 presidential primary campaigns, critics charged that some of the passages reflected racist, anti-Semitic, and homophobic bigotry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drno_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-drno-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chron96_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chron96-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMN96_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMN96-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> In a 1996 interview, Paul did not deny writing the newsletters and defended some of their contents, but specified that he opposes racism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> In March 2001, Paul said he did not write the commentaries, but stopped short of denying authorship in 1996 because his campaign advisers had thought it would be too confusing and that he had to live with the material published under his name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TM_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-TM-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> In 2011 Paul's spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Benton" title="Jesse Benton">Jesse Benton</a> said Paul had "taken moral responsibility because they appeared under his name and slipped through under his watch".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackie_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackie-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-congressional_career">Post-congressional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Post-congressional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In April 2013, Paul founded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ron_Paul_Institute_for_Peace_and_Prosperity" title="Ron Paul Institute for Peace and Prosperity">Ron Paul Institute for Peace and Prosperity</a>, a foreign policy <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a> that seeks to promote his non-interventionist views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The institute is part of his larger foundation <a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Rational_Economics_and_Education" title="Foundation for Rational Economics and Education">Foundation for Rational Economics and Education</a>.</p>
<p>In the same month, he began to offer the <i>Ron Paul Curriculum</i>, a homeschool online curriculum developed by <a href="/wiki/Gary_North_(economist)" title="Gary North (economist)">Gary North</a> and taught from a "free market and Christian" perspective; it is free from grades <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a>–5 and available to paid members from 6–12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2013, Paul criticized the <a href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">NSA surveillance program</a> and praised <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> for having performed a "great service to the American people by exposing the truth about what our government is doing in secret".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ron_Paul_Channel">Ron Paul Channel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Ron Paul Channel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, Paul established the "Ron Paul Channel", an Internet broadcast. Its slogan is "Turn Off Your TV. Turn On the Truth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Speaking about the channel, Paul said, "I was at a debate one time a couple years ago, where I didn't think I got a fair shake. In a two-hour debate, I had 89 seconds. I thought, maybe there's something wrong with the media. Maybe they're not covering us fairly. I'm just using it as a pun, but there’s a bit of truth to this. We don't get a fair shake. The people who believe in liberty and limited government don't expect it from the ordinary media." Speaking about his youth appeal, he noted, "They don’t sit and watch TV and turn the programs on at seven o'clock to watch us like that – so I thought the technology was there. The country is ripe for the continuation of this revolution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2015, Ron Paul ended all relationships with the <i>Voices of Liberty</i> and the Ron Paul Channel to start a new internet broadcast called the Ron Paul Liberty Report. According to Paul himself, it will not cost a thing, unlike the previous Ron Paul Channel. In the announcement of the ended relationship, Paul said, "But the message I have always tried to deliver over the years has always been the same, and that is spreading the message of liberty. Right now I am very much engaged in doing that through the internet. But, I believe we can do better. Right now, the program has changed to the <i>Ron Paul Liberty Report</i>, and that is what we do, we report on liberty in context of what is going on in daily activity and what is going on in the news." Paul went on to say that it will be more locally controlled, unlike the previous Ron Paul Channel. Paul continued to say it will be produced out of Texas, instead of California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spokesman_for_Stansberry_Research">Spokesman for Stansberry Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Spokesman for Stansberry Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2015, Paul began appearing in <a href="/wiki/Infomercial" title="Infomercial">infomercials</a> warning about an upcoming financial meltdown as a result of the imminent crash of the world’s currencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apocalypse_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-apocalypse-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Financial_Crisis_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Financial_Crisis-205">[205]</a></sup> He urges listeners to read <i>America 2020: The Survival Blueprint</i>, a book written by <a href="/wiki/Porter_Stansberry" title="Porter Stansberry">Porter Stansberry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEC_suit_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-SEC_suit-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Presidential_Election">2016 Presidential Election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 2016 Presidential Election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Paul received 1 electoral vote from a Texas <a href="/wiki/Faithless_elector" title="Faithless elector">faithless elector</a> (who had been pledged to <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>) in the 2016 presidential election,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimesElectoralCollege_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimesElectoralCollege-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texas_Tribune_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Texas_Tribune-208">[208]</a></sup> making Paul the oldest person ever to receive an electoral vote.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ron_Paul&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Will,_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg/220px-Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg/330px-Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg/440px-Will%2C_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Will,_Rand_%26_Ron_Paul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Paul at a rally in <a href="/wiki/Erlanger,_Kentucky" title="Erlanger, Kentucky">Erlanger, Kentucky</a>, on October 2, 2010, along with his son, Senator <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">Rand Paul</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, and his grandson, William Paul <i>(pictured from right to left)</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Paul has been married to Carol (Carolyn) Wells since 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailypaul_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailypaul-209">[209]</a></sup> They met in 1952 when Wells asked Paul to be her escort to her 16th birthday party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> They have five children, who were <a href="/wiki/Infant_baptism" title="Infant baptism">baptized</a> <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopalian</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ny_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-ny-13">[13]</a></sup> Ronald, Lori, <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">Randal</a>, Robert, and Joy. Paul's son Randal is the junior United States senator from the state of Kentucky. Raised a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, Paul later became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Since 1995, Carol Paul has published the <i><a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul_Family_Cookbook" title="Ron Paul Family Cookbook">Ron Paul Family Cookbook</a></i>, a collection of recipes she and her friends contributed, and which was sold in part to support Ron Paul's political campaigns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> His life and career is the subject of the 2012 film <i>Ron Paul Uprising</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul and his wife currently reside in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Jackson,_Texas" title="Lake Jackson, Texas">Lake Jackson, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>

<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
